The CRI is a critical abstraction layer that allows Kubernetes to be agnostic about the underlying container runtime, with containerd being the most widely adopted implementation.\n\n**Key Finding:** The architecture is cleanly separated:\n- **Kubernetes owns and defines the CRI contract** via Protocol Buffer files\n- **Proto compiler generates Go types and gRPC stubs** for the service interface\n- **Kubernetes vendorizes containerd's API types** for compatibility and reference\n- **containerd implements the RuntimeService interface** within its plugin system\n- **gRPC bridges Kubernetes kubelet and containerd daemon** across process boundaries\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Kubernetes CRI API Definition\n\n### 1.1 Source File Location\n\n**Primary Source:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto`\n\n- **Size:** 2,129 lines\n- **Authority:** Kubernetes project (owned by Kubernetes/Kubernetes)\n- **Version Control:** Committed to Kubernetes source tree\n- **Generated From:** Protocol Buffer 3 (.proto) format\n- **Purpose:** Defines the complete contract between Kubernetes kubelet and any container runtime\n\n### 1.2 RuntimeService Complete RPC Interface\n\nThe CRI RuntimeService defines **32 RPC methods** across 6 operational categories:\n\n#### Category 1: Pod Sandbox Lifecycle (5 methods)\nPod sandboxes are the Kubernetes abstraction for a pod—they provide the namespace and infrastructure that containers run within.\n\n```\nrpc Version(VersionRequest) returns (VersionResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Runtime identification and version negotiation\n  └─ Request: apiVersion string\n  └─ Response: name, version, apiVersion\n\nrpc RunPodSandbox(RunPodSandboxRequest) returns (RunPodSandboxResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Create and start a pod-level sandbox\n  └─ Request: config (PodSandboxConfig), runtime_handler (string)\n  └─ Response: pod_sandbox_id (string)\n  └─ Key Action: Creates network namespace, init container environment\n\nrpc StopPodSandbox(StopPodSandboxRequest) returns (StopPodSandboxResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Stop a running sandbox (graceful, preserves state)\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id (string)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Key Action: Stops containers, releases network, preserves data\n\nrpc RemovePodSandbox(RemovePodSandboxRequest) returns (RemovePodSandboxResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Remove sandbox and all resources (terminal operation)\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id (string)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Key Action: Cleanup leases, tear down network, delete all containers\n\nrpc PodSandboxStatus(PodSandboxStatusRequest) returns (PodSandboxStatusResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Query sandbox status and network information\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id (string), verbose (bool)\n  └─ Response: status (PodSandboxStatus)\n  └─ Returns: ID, metadata, state (Ready|NotReady), timestamps, network status\n\nrpc ListPodSandbox(ListPodSandboxRequest) returns (ListPodSandboxResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Enumerate all sandboxes with optional filtering\n  └─ Request: filter (PodSandboxFilter), optional max_results\n  └─ Response: items[] (PodSandboxListItem)\n  └─ Supports filtering by: ID, namespace, name labels, and state\n```\n\n**Pod Sandbox State Machine:**\n```\nUnknown/Initial\n    ↓ (RunPodSandbox succeeds)\nReady (fully functional, containers can run)\n    ↓ (StopPodSandbox called)\nNotReady (stopped, resources reserved)\n    ↓ (RemovePodSandbox called)\nRemoved (all resources freed)\n```\n\n#### Category 2: Container Lifecycle (6 methods)\nContainers are child processes/tasks running within a pod sandbox.\n\n```\nrpc CreateContainer(CreateContainerRequest) returns (CreateContainerResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Create a new container in given PodSandbox\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id, config (ContainerConfig), sandbox_config\n  └─ Response: container_id (string)\n  └─ Note: Does NOT start the container, only prepares it\n\nrpc StartContainer(StartContainerRequest) returns (StartContainerResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Start a previously created container\n  └─ Request: container_id (string)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Prerequisite: CreateContainer must have been called first\n\nrpc StopContainer(StopContainerRequest) returns (StopContainerResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Stop a running container with grace period\n  └─ Request: container_id, timeout (int64 seconds)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Behavior: SIGTERM, wait timeout, then SIGKILL if needed\n\nrpc RemoveContainer(RemoveContainerRequest) returns (RemoveContainerResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Remove container and all associated resources\n  └─ Request: container_id (string)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Side effects: Forcibly stops if still running, cleans logs, removes snapshots\n\nrpc ListContainers(ListContainersRequest) returns (ListContainersResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Enumerate all containers with optional filtering\n  └─ Request: filter (ContainerFilter), max_results (int)\n  └─ Response: containers[] (Container)\n  └─ Filters: ID, pod_sandbox_id, state, labels\n\nrpc ContainerStatus(ContainerStatusRequest) returns (ContainerStatusResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get detailed container status and metadata\n  └─ Request: container_id, verbose (bool)\n  └─ Response: status (ContainerStatus)\n  └─ Returns: ID, metadata, state, timestamps, exit code, image ref, user info\n```\n\n**Container State Machine:**\n```\nCreated (prepared, not yet running)\n    ↓ (StartContainer called)\nRunning (process executing)\n    ├─ (normal exit, signal, OOM, etc.)\n    ↓\nExited (process terminated, exit code available)\n    ↓ (RemoveContainer called)\nRemoved (all resources freed)\n\nUnknown state: Reserved for error conditions\n```\n\n#### Category 3: Container Operations (4 methods)\nIn-container operations for execution and resource management.\n\n```\nrpc UpdateContainerResources(UpdateContainerResourcesRequest) returns (UpdateContainerResourcesResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Change container's resource limits dynamically\n  └─ Request: container_id, resources (LinuxContainerResources)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Supports: CPU quota/period, memory limit, swap, OOM behavior\n  └─ Note: Applied synchronously (immediately effective)\n\nrpc ReopenContainerLog(ReopenContainerLogRequest) returns (ReopenContainerLogResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Reopen stdout/stderr log files (for log rotation)\n  └─ Request: container_id (string)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Use case: kubelet rotates logs, container needs to flush and reopen\n\nrpc ExecSync(ExecSyncRequest) returns (ExecSyncResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Run command in container, wait for completion (synchronous)\n  └─ Request: container_id, cmd[], timeout, stderr (bool)\n  └─ Response: stdout (bytes), stderr (bytes), exit_code (int)\n  └─ Behavior: Blocks until command exits or timeout\n  └─ Used by: kubelet health checks (liveness/readiness probes)\n\nrpc Exec(ExecRequest) returns (ExecResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Prepare bidirectional streaming endpoint for command execution\n  └─ Request: container_id, cmd[], stdin/stdout/stderr (bool), tty (bool)\n  └─ Response: url (string to streaming endpoint)\n  └─ Protocol: Upgrades to WebSocket or raw TCP for streaming\n  └─ Used by: kubectl exec command\n```\n\n#### Category 4: Streaming Operations (2 methods)\nHandle bidirectional streaming for interactive sessions.\n\n```\nrpc Attach(AttachRequest) returns (AttachResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Prepare streaming endpoint to attach to running container\n  └─ Request: container_id, stdin/stdout/stderr (bool), tty (bool)\n  └─ Response: url (string to streaming endpoint)\n  └─ Protocol: WebSocket or raw TCP streaming\n  └─ Used by: kubectl attach command\n\nrpc PortForward(PortForwardRequest) returns (PortForwardResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Prepare streaming endpoint for port forwarding\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id, ports[] (int32)\n  └─ Response: url (string to streaming endpoint)\n  └─ Protocol: Streaming protocol for TCP traffic forwarding\n  └─ Used by: kubectl port-forward command\n```\n\n#### Category 5: Statistics and Monitoring (4 methods)\nRuntime and container metrics collection.\n\n```\nrpc ContainerStats(ContainerStatsRequest) returns (ContainerStatsResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get CPU/memory statistics for single container\n  └─ Request: container_id (string)\n  └─ Response: stats (ContainerStats)\n  └─ Metrics: cpu_usage_cores, memory_usage_bytes, timestamps\n  └─ Used by: kubectl top pods, metrics-server\n\nrpc ListContainerStats(ListContainerStatsRequest) returns (ListContainerStatsResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get statistics for all containers matching filter\n  └─ Request: filter (ContainerStatsFilter), max_results\n  └─ Response: stats[] (ContainerStats)\n  └─ Efficiency: Bulk retrieval more efficient than N individual calls\n\nrpc PodSandboxStats(PodSandboxStatsRequest) returns (PodSandboxStatsResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get aggregated statistics for entire pod sandbox\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id (string)\n  └─ Response: stats (PodSandboxStats)\n\nrpc ListPodSandboxStats(ListPodSandboxStatsRequest) returns (ListPodSandboxStatsResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get pod-level statistics for all sandboxes\n  └─ Request: filter (PodSandboxStatsFilter), max_results\n  └─ Response: stats[] (PodSandboxStats)\n```\n\n#### Category 6: Runtime Configuration and Status (4 methods)\n\n```\nrpc Status(StatusRequest) returns (StatusResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get overall runtime status and readiness\n  └─ Request: verbose (bool)\n  └─ Response: status (RuntimeStatus)\n  └─ Fields: conditions[] (RuntimeCondition), metadata\n  └─ Used by: kubelet startup checks, runtime readiness probes\n\nrpc RuntimeConfig(RuntimeConfigRequest) returns (RuntimeConfigResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Query current runtime configuration\n  └─ Request: (empty)\n  └─ Response: runtime_config (RuntimeConfig)\n  └─ Returns: Configured memory/cpu resources, supported features\n\nrpc UpdateRuntimeConfig(UpdateRuntimeConfigRequest) returns (UpdateRuntimeConfigResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Reconfigure runtime parameters without restart\n  └─ Request: runtime_config (RuntimeConfig)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Examples: Network config, RLIMIT settings\n\nrpc UpdatePodSandboxResources(UpdatePodSandboxResourcesRequest) returns (UpdatePodSandboxResourcesResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Update pod-level resource configuration (cgroup limits)\n  └─ Request: pod_sandbox_id, resources (LinuxPodSandboxResources)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Supports: CPU/memory/swap limits, OOM behavior\n```\n\n#### Category 7: Events and Checkpointing (2 methods)\n\n```\nrpc GetContainerEvents(GetContainerEventsRequest) returns (stream ContainerEventResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Stream container lifecycle events\n  └─ Request: filter (ContainerEventFilter)\n  └─ Response: stream of ContainerEventResponse\n  └─ Events: Created, Started, Stopped, Deleted, Paused, Resumed\n  └─ Used by: kubelet event watches, audit logging\n\nrpc CheckpointContainer(CheckpointContainerRequest) returns (CheckpointContainerResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Create checkpoint of container state (CRIU integration)\n  └─ Request: container_id, checkpoint_path, export (bool)\n  └─ Response: (empty)\n  └─ Use case: Container migration, live update\n```\n\n#### Category 8: Metrics (2 methods)\n\n```\nrpc ListMetricDescriptors(ListMetricDescriptorsRequest) returns (ListMetricDescriptorsResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get metadata about available metrics\n  └─ Request: (empty)\n  └─ Response: descriptors[] (MetricDescriptor)\n  └─ Fields: name, help, unit, type\n\nrpc ListPodSandboxMetrics(ListPodSandboxMetricsRequest) returns (ListPodSandboxMetricsResponse)\n  └─ Purpose: Get pod-level metrics (advanced monitoring)\n  └─ Request: filter (PodSandboxMetricsFilter)\n  └─ Response: resources[] (PodSandboxMetrics)\n```\n\n### 1.3 Key Message Type Definitions\n\n#### PodSandboxConfig (Lines 474-521)\nMessage that defines the pod environment:\n```\nmessage PodSandboxConfig {\n    PodSandboxMetadata metadata = 1;  // Name, UID, namespace, attempt\n    string hostname = 2;              // Pod hostname\n    string log_directory = 3;         // Where to write pod logs\n    DNSConfig dns_config = 4;         // /etc/resolv.conf equivalent\n    repeated PortMapping port_mappings = 5;  // Port forwarding rules\n    map<string, string> labels = 6;   // Kubernetes labels\n    map<string, string> annotations = 7;  // Kubernetes annotations\n    LinuxPodSandboxConfig linux = 8;  // Linux-specific config\n    WindowsPodSandboxConfig windows = 9;  // Windows-specific config\n}\n```\n\n#### ContainerConfig (Lines 1134-1195)\nMessage that defines a container:\n```\nmessage ContainerConfig {\n    ContainerMetadata metadata = 1;   // Name, attempt\n    ImageSpec image = 2;              // Image to run\n    repeated string command = 3;      // Entrypoint\n    repeated string args = 4;         // Arguments\n    string working_dir = 5;           // Working directory\n    repeated KeyValue envs = 6;       // Environment variables\n    repeated Mount mounts = 7;        // Volume mounts\n    repeated Device devices = 8;      // Device access (/dev/*)\n    map<string, string> labels = 9;   // Labels\n    map<string, string> annotations = 10;  // Annotations\n    string log_path = 11;             // Where to write logs\n    bool stdin = 12;                  // Attach stdin\n    bool stdin_once = 13;             // Close stdin after first attach\n    bool tty = 14;                    // TTY mode\n    LinuxContainerConfig linux = 15;  // Linux-specific\n    WindowsContainerConfig windows = 16;  // Windows-specific\n    repeated CDIDevice cdi_devices = 17;  // CDI device requests\n    Signal stop_signal = 18;          // Signal for graceful stop\n}\n```\n\n#### PodSandboxStatus (Lines 592-614)\nRuntime representation of pod state:\n```\nmessage PodSandboxStatus {\n    string id = 1;\n    PodSandboxMetadata metadata = 2;\n    PodSandboxState state = 3;       // Ready, NotReady, Unknown\n    int64 created_at = 4;            // Nanosecond timestamp\n    PodSandboxNetworkStatus network = 5;  // IP, interfaces, routes\n    LinuxPodSandboxStatus linux = 6; // Linux info: cgroup, security context\n    map<string, string> labels = 7;\n    map<string, string> annotations = 8;\n    string runtime_handler = 9;      // Which sandbox controller\n}\n```\n\n#### ContainerStatus (Lines 1389-1440)\nRuntime representation of container state:\n```\nmessage ContainerStatus {\n    string id = 1;\n    ContainerMetadata metadata = 2;\n    ContainerState state = 3;         // Created, Running, Exited, Unknown\n    int64 created_at = 4;\n    int64 started_at = 5;\n    int64 finished_at = 6;\n    int32 exit_code = 7;              // Only if state=Exited\n    string reason = 8;                // OOMKilled, Error, etc.\n    string message = 9;               // Error message\n    ImageSpec image = 10;\n    string image_ref = 11;            // Resolved image ID\n    string image_id = 12;             // Content hash\n    ContainerUser user = 13;          // UID/GID info\n    Signal stop_signal = 14;          // SIGTERM, etc.\n}\n```\n\n### 1.4 Generated Go Types\n\nThe Protocol Buffer compiler generates Go code from `api.proto`:\n\n**Generated Files:**\n- `api.pb.go` - ~583 KB\n  - Message struct definitions (PodSandboxConfig, ContainerConfig, etc.)\n  - Protobuf marshaling/unmarshaling (Proto() methods)\n  - Reflection metadata\n  - Approximately 9,500+ lines of generated code\n\n- `api_grpc.pb.go` - ~79 KB\n  - gRPC service interfaces (RuntimeServiceClient, RuntimeServiceServer)\n  - gRPC method stubs with request/response types\n  - Approximately 1,200+ lines\n\n**Compiler Used:**\n- `protoc` v4.23.4\n- `protoc-gen-go` v1.36.4\n- `protoc-gen-go-grpc` v1.5.1\n\n### 1.5 Service Interface Definitions (Go)\n\nKubernetes also provides hand-written Go interfaces in `services.go`:\n\n```go\n// RuntimeVersioner handles version negotiation\ntype RuntimeVersioner interface {\n    Version(ctx context.Context, apiVersion string) (*runtimeapi.VersionResponse, error)\n}\n\n// ContainerManager operations\ntype ContainerManager interface {\n    CreateContainer(ctx context.Context, podSandboxID string, config *runtimeapi.ContainerConfig, ...) (string, error)\n    StartContainer(ctx context.Context, containerID string) error\n    StopContainer(ctx context.Context, containerID string, timeout int64) error\n    RemoveContainer(ctx context.Context, containerID string) error\n    ListContainers(ctx context.Context, filter *runtimeapi.ContainerFilter) ([]*runtimeapi.Container, error)\n    ContainerStatus(ctx context.Context, containerID string, ...) (*runtimeapi.ContainerStatus, error)\n    // ... more methods ...\n}\n\n// PodSandboxManager operations\ntype PodSandboxManager interface {\n    RunPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, config *runtimeapi.PodSandboxConfig, ...) (string, error)\n    StopPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, podSandboxID string) error\n    RemovePodSandbox(ctx context.Context, podSandboxID string) error\n    PodSandboxStatus(ctx context.Context, podSandboxID string, ...) (*runtimeapi.PodSandboxStatus, error)\n    ListPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, filter *runtimeapi.PodSandboxFilter) ([]*runtimeapi.PodSandboxListItem, error)\n    // ... more methods ...\n}\n\n// Composed interface that all runtimes must implement\ntype RuntimeService interface {\n    RuntimeVersioner\n    ContainerManager\n    PodSandboxManager\n    ContainerStatsManager\n    UpdateRuntimeConfig(ctx context.Context, runtimeConfig *runtimeapi.RuntimeConfig) error\n    Status(ctx context.Context, verbose bool) (*runtimeapi.StatusResponse, error)\n    RuntimeConfig(ctx context.Context) (*runtimeapi.RuntimeConfigResponse, error)\n    Close() error\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Containerd Implementation\n\n### 2.1 Architecture Overview\n\nContainerd implements the CRI as a **plugin** within its architecture. It doesn't inherit or reimport Kubernetes types; instead, it:\n1. Receives gRPC requests from Kubernetes kubelet\n2. Converts them to containerd's internal data structures\n3. Performs operations using containerd's core APIs\n4. Returns responses back through gRPC\n\n**Containerd CRI Plugin Structure:**\n```\ncontainerd (daemon)\n├── Plugin System (plugin.Plugin interface)\n│   └── CRI Plugin (type \"cri\", ID \"cri\")\n│       ├── RuntimeServiceServer (implements CRI gRPC)\n│       ├── ImageServiceServer (implements CRI gRPC)\n│       └── Dependencies:\n│           ├── containerd.Client (core API)\n│           ├── Sandbox Controllers (pod implementation)\n│           ├── Snapshot Service (storage)\n│           ├── Content Store (image storage)\n│           ├── Task Service (container processes)\n│           └── Leases Service (resource cleanup)\n```\n\n### 2.2 Plugin Registration (cri.go)\n\n**File:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/plugins/cri/cri.go`\n\nThe plugin entry point defines how containerd loads the CRI:\n\n```go\nfunc init() {\n    registry.Register(&plugin.Registration{\n        Type:     plugins.GRPCPlugin,  // Type of plugin\n        ID:       \"cri\",               // Plugin identifier\n        Requires: []string{             // Dependencies\n            plugins.CRIServicePlugin,\n            plugins.SandboxControllerPlugin,\n            plugins.EventPlugin,\n            plugins.LeasePlugin,\n            // ... more\n        },\n        InitFn: initCRIService,  // Initialization function\n    })\n}\n\nfunc initCRIService(ic *plugin.InitContext) (interface{}, error) {\n    // Called by containerd to initialize CRI plugin\n    // 1. Retrieves dependent plugins\n    // 2. Creates new CRIService instance\n    // 3. Returns service ready for gRPC registration\n}\n```\n\n**gRPC Registration:**\nAfter the plugin is initialized, containerd automatically:\n1. Casts the returned service to `RuntimeServiceServer`\n2. Casts the returned service to `ImageServiceServer`\n3. Registers both onto the gRPC server\n4. Listens on Unix socket (default: /run/containerd/containerd.sock)\n\n### 2.3 Core Service Implementation (service.go)\n\n**File:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/service.go` (1,200+ lines)\n\n**CRIService Interface (what containerd's CRI must implement):**\n```go\ntype CRIService interface {\n    io.Closer\n    IsInitialized() bool\n    Run(ready func()) error\n}\n```\n\n**criService Struct (the actual implementation):**\n```go\ntype criService struct {\n    config              *config.Config         // CRI configuration\n    client              *containerd.Client     // Core containerd client\n\n    // State stores\n    sandboxStore        *sandbox.Store         // Pod sandbox metadata\n    containerStore      *container.Store       // Container metadata\n\n    // Name management\n    sandboxNameIndex    registrar.Registrar    // Unique pod names\n    containerNameIndex  registrar.Registrar    // Unique container names\n\n    // Networking\n    netPlugin           map[string]cni.CNI     // CNI plugins (one per subnet)\n\n    // Streaming (exec/logs/attach)\n    streamServer        streaming.Server       // HTTP server for streaming\n\n    // Event handling\n    eventMonitor        *eventmonitor.EventMonitor  // Watches containerd events\n\n    // Pod control\n    sandboxService      *criSandboxService     // Delegates to controllers\n\n    // Statistics\n    statsCollector      *statsCollector        // Background stats\n}\n```\n\n**Key Methods:**\n\n1. **NewCRIService() → *criService**\n   - Creates new service instance\n   - Loads configuration\n   - Initializes data stores\n   - Sets up networking\n   - Returns ready-to-use service\n\n2. **Run(ready func()) error**\n   - Starts background components:\n     - Event monitor goroutine (watches containerd events)\n     - Streaming server (handles exec/logs/attach)\n     - Stats collector (background CPU metrics)\n     - State recovery (reconstructs state from containerd)\n   - Calls ready() callback when fully initialized\n   - Blocks while running\n\n3. **Close() error**\n   - Graceful shutdown:\n     - Stops event monitor\n     - Closes streaming server\n     - Closes statistics collector\n     - Closes containerd client\n     - Closes network plugins\n\n4. **IsInitialized() bool**\n   - Returns true once Run() has completed initialization\n\n### 2.4 Pod Sandbox Implementation\n\n#### RunPodSandbox (sandbox_run.go)\n\nMaps Kubernetes CRI RunPodSandboxRequest to containerd operations:\n\n```\nInput: RunPodSandboxRequest {\n    config: PodSandboxConfig { ... }\n    runtime_handler: \"runc\"\n}\n\nStep 1: Generate unique pod sandbox ID (128-bit UUID)\nStep 2: Reserve pod name in sandboxNameIndex\n        (prevents duplicate names, enforces uniqueness)\n\nStep 3: Create containerd lease\n        (lease tracks resources that belong to this pod\n         when pod is deleted, all leased objects are cleaned up)\n\nStep 4: Retrieve OCI runtime configuration\n        (e.g., runc, kata, gvisor - based on runtime_handler)\n\nStep 5: Create sandbox object with metadata\n        (contains config, ID, name, created timestamp)\n\nStep 6: Store sandbox in sandboxStore\n        (in-memory map, allows fast lookups)\n\nStep 7: Setup networking\n        (run CNI plugin to allocate IP address, setup veth pairs,\n         create network namespace)\n\nStep 8: Create sandbox via sandboxService\n        (delegates to platform-specific controller:\n         Linux: runc-based sandbox controller\n         Windows: Windows Container controller\n         etc.)\n\nStep 9: Mark sandbox as \"ready\" in status\n        (set state=Ready, populate network status with IPs)\n\nOutput: RunPodSandboxResponse {\n    pod_sandbox_id: \"abc123def456...\"\n}\n```\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `sandbox_run.go` - RunPodSandbox implementation\n- `sandbox.go` - Helper functions\n- `store/sandbox/sandbox.go` - Sandbox metadata store\n\n**containerd Interaction:**\n```go\n// Get platform-specific sandbox controller\ncontroller := s.sandboxService.Get(runtimeHandler)\n\n// Create sandbox metadata\nsandbox := &sandbox.Sandbox{\n    Metadata: &sandbox.Metadata{\n        ID: sandboxID,\n        Config: config,\n        RuntimeHandler: runtimeHandler,\n    },\n}\n\n// Start sandbox (runs sandbox container)\ntask, err := controller.StartSandbox(ctx, sandbox)\n\n// Store in memory\ns.sandboxStore.Add(sandbox)\n```\n\n#### StopPodSandbox (sandbox_stop.go)\n\nGraceful termination of pod:\n\n```\nInput: StopPodSandboxRequest { pod_sandbox_id: \"abc123...\" }\n\nStep 1: Look up sandbox from store\n        (fail silently if not found - idempotent)\n\nStep 2: Get all containers in sandbox\n        (from containerStore, filter by sandbox_id)\n\nStep 3: Force-stop all containers\n        (call StopContainer with timeout=0 for each)\n\nStep 4: Stop sandbox task\n        (send SIGTERM to sandbox container,\n         wait timeout, send SIGKILL if needed)\n\nStep 5: Update sandbox state to \"NotReady\"\n        (containers can no longer run in this sandbox\n         but sandbox resources are still reserved)\n\nOutput: StopPodSandboxResponse { }\n```\n\n**Idempotency:**\nIf sandbox is already stopped, returns success immediately (no error).\n\n#### RemovePodSandbox (sandbox_remove.go)\n\nComplete cleanup and resource deallocation:\n\n```\nInput: RemovePodSandboxRequest { pod_sandbox_id: \"abc123...\" }\n\nStep 1: Look up sandbox (fail silently if not found - idempotent)\n\nStep 2: If still running, forcibly stop it\n        (calls StopPodSandbox internally)\n\nStep 3: Remove all containers in sandbox\n        (forcibly, including their resources)\n\nStep 4: Call ShutdownSandbox on controller\n        (platform-specific cleanup:\n         Linux: remove cgroup, unmount filesystems\n         Windows: cleanup container state)\n\nStep 5: Close network namespace\n        (cleanup veth pairs, release IP address via CNI teardown)\n\nStep 6: Delete containerd lease\n        (automatically garbage collects any remaining\n         containerd objects created under this lease)\n\nStep 7: Remove from sandboxNameIndex\n        (free the name for reuse)\n\nStep 8: Remove from sandboxStore\n        (delete from in-memory map)\n\nOutput: RemovePodSandboxResponse { }\n```\n\n### 2.5 Container Implementation\n\n#### CreateContainer (container_create.go)\n\nPrepare container for execution (but don't start it):\n\n```\nInput: CreateContainerRequest {\n    pod_sandbox_id: \"abc123...\"\n    config: ContainerConfig { ... }\n    sandbox_config: PodSandboxConfig { ... }\n}\n\nStep 1: Look up parent sandbox\n        (fail with error if not found)\n\nStep 2: Verify sandbox is Ready\n        (containers can only run in ready sandboxes)\n\nStep 3: Generate unique container ID\n\nStep 4: Reserve container name\n        (in containerNameIndex)\n\nStep 5: Resolve image\n        (pull if needed, get image config)\n\nStep 6: Build OCI runtime spec\n        (convert CRI ContainerConfig to OCI spec:\n         - set process args\n         - set environment variables\n         - setup mounts\n         - set resource limits\n         - set security context\n         - apply SELinux labels, AppArmor profiles)\n\nStep 7: Create containerd container\n        (s.client.NewContainer() with OCI spec)\n\nStep 8: Store in containerStore\n        (for future lookups)\n\nOutput: CreateContainerResponse {\n    container_id: \"xyz789...\"\n}\n```\n\n**Key Point:** Container is created but NOT started. This allows kubelet to set up any pre-start hooks before StartContainer is called.\n\n#### StartContainer (container_start.go)\n\nBegin container execution:\n\n```\nInput: StartContainerRequest { container_id: \"xyz789...\" }\n\nStep 1: Look up container from store\n\nStep 2: Look up parent sandbox\n        (verify it's still Ready)\n\nStep 3: Set container state to \"Starting\"\n\nStep 4: Create logger (for stdout/stderr)\n\nStep 5: Setup container I/O\n        (create pipes/files for stdin/stdout/stderr)\n\nStep 6: Start container task\n        (containerd.Container.NewTask(ctx, io, opts))\n        This:\n        - Allocates container process ID\n        - Sets up namespaces (pid, ipc, uts, network)\n        - Mounts filesystems\n        - Sets resource limits\n        - Starts container process (runs entry command)\n\nStep 7: Publish \"ContainerStarted\" event\n        (for event watchers)\n\nStep 8: Update container state to \"Running\"\n\nOutput: StartContainerResponse { }\n```\n\n#### StopContainer (container_stop.go)\n\nGraceful termination:\n\n```\nInput: StopContainerRequest {\n    container_id: \"xyz789...\"\n    timeout: 30  (seconds)\n}\n\nStep 1: Look up container (fail silently - idempotent)\n\nStep 2: If already stopped, return success\n\nStep 3: Send SIGTERM to container process\n        (give it timeout seconds to shutdown)\n\nStep 4: Wait for exit\n        (container.Task.Wait() with timeout)\n\nStep 5: If timeout expires, send SIGKILL\n        (force termination)\n\nStep 6: Update container state to \"Exited\"\n\nStep 7: Record exit code and exit timestamp\n\nOutput: StopContainerResponse { }\n\nNote: Handles race conditions with automatic retry on\n      \"connection closed\" errors (containerd restarted)\n```\n\n#### RemoveContainer (container_remove.go)\n\nComplete cleanup:\n\n```\nInput: RemoveContainerRequest { container_id: \"xyz789...\" }\n\nStep 1: Look up container (fail silently - idempotent)\n\nStep 2: If still running, forcibly stop it\n\nStep 3: Delete containerd container\n        (s.client.LoadContainer().Delete())\n\nStep 4: Clean up I/O\n        (close stdin/stdout/stderr pipes)\n\nStep 5: Remove snapshot\n        (delete root filesystem diff)\n\nStep 6: Release container lease\n\nStep 7: Remove from containerNameIndex\n\nStep 8: Remove from containerStore\n\nOutput: RemoveContainerResponse { }\n```\n\n### 2.6 Sandbox Service Abstraction (sandbox_service.go)\n\nContainerd abstracts pod sandbox implementation via sandboxers:\n\n```go\ntype criSandboxService struct {\n    controllers map[string]sandbox.Controller  // runtime_handler → controller\n}\n\n// Controllers are platform-specific:\n// \"runc\" → Linux container sandbox\n// \"kata\" → Kata Containers sandbox\n// \"gvisor\" → gVisor container runtime\n// etc.\n```\n\n**Methods that delegate to controllers:**\n\n```\nCreateSandbox(ctx context.Context, sandbox *sandbox.Sandbox) error\n  → controller.CreateSandbox(ctx, sandbox)\n\nStartSandbox(ctx context.Context, sandbox *sandbox.Sandbox) (Task, error)\n  → controller.StartSandbox(ctx, sandbox)\n\nStopSandbox(ctx context.Context, sandbox *sandbox.Sandbox) error\n  → controller.StopSandbox(ctx, sandbox)\n\nShutdownSandbox(ctx context.Context, sandbox *sandbox.Sandbox) error\n  → controller.ShutdownSandbox(ctx, sandbox)\n\nSandboxStatus(ctx context.Context, sandboxID string) (SandboxStatus, error)\n  → controller.SandboxStatus(ctx, sandboxID)\n```\n\n### 2.7 Data Stores\n\n#### Sandbox Store (store/sandbox/sandbox.go)\n\n**Purpose:** In-memory cache of sandbox state\n\n```go\ntype Sandbox struct {\n    // Immutable (set at creation)\n    Metadata *Metadata  // ID, Name, Config, RuntimeHandler\n\n    // Mutable (updated during lifecycle)\n    Status *Status      // State (Ready/NotReady), Pid, ExitCode\n\n    // Resources\n    Container containerd.Container  // Reference to containerd container\n    Sandboxer string                // Which controller\n    NetNS     *netns.NetNS          // Network namespace handle\n}\n\ntype Metadata struct {\n    ID             string\n    Name           string\n    Config         *runtimeapi.PodSandboxConfig\n    RuntimeHandler string\n    Attempt        uint32\n}\n\ntype Status struct {\n    State     PodSandboxState  // Ready, NotReady\n    Pid       uint32\n    ExitCode  int32\n    ExitedAt  int64  // Nanoseconds\n}\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n- `Add(sandbox *Sandbox)` - Store in memory\n- `Get(id string) *Sandbox` - Retrieve by ID\n- `List(filter ...) []*Sandbox` - Query with filters\n- `Delete(id string)` - Remove from memory\n- `UpdateContainerStats(id string, stats ...)` - Update stats\n\n#### Container Store (store/container/container.go)\n\n**Purpose:** In-memory cache of container state\n\n```go\ntype Container struct {\n    // Immutable\n    Metadata *Metadata  // ID, Name, SandboxID, Config\n\n    // Mutable\n    Status *Status      // State (Created/Running/Exited), Pid, ExitCode\n\n    // Resources\n    Container containerd.Container  // Reference to containerd container\n    IO        *cio.ContainerIO      // Stdin/stdout/stderr\n}\n\ntype Metadata struct {\n    ID        string\n    Name      string\n    SandboxID string\n    Config    *runtimeapi.ContainerConfig\n    ImageRef  string\n}\n\ntype Status struct {\n    State      ContainerState  // Created, Running, Exited\n    Pid        uint32\n    ExitCode   int32\n    CreatedAt  int64\n    StartedAt  int64\n    FinishedAt int64\n}\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n- `Add(container *Container)` - Store\n- `Get(id string) *Container` - Retrieve\n- `List(filter ...) []*Container` - Query\n- `Delete(id string)` - Remove\n- `GetContainers(podID string) []*Container` - Get all in pod\n\n### 2.8 Supporting Components\n\n#### Streaming Server (streamingserver/)\nHandles bidirectional streaming for:\n- `Exec()` - Command execution\n- `Attach()` - Container attachment\n- `PortForward()` - Port forwarding\n\nHTTP server listening on localhost (kubelet connects locally).\n\n#### Event Monitor (server/events/)\nSubscribes to containerd's event stream:\n- Container created, started, stopped, deleted\n- Image pulled\n- OOM events\n\nPropagates as CRI `ContainerEventResponse` stream.\n\n#### Stats Collector (server/stats_collector.go)\nBackground goroutine that periodically:\n- Reads container CPU stats from cgroup\n- Calculates UsageNanoCores metric\n- Caches for ContainerStats/ListContainerStats queries\n\n#### NRI Integration (server/nri/)\nHooks for Node Resource Interface:\n- Allows external plugins to modify pod/container specs\n- Called before creating sandbox/container\n- Can be used for resource allocation, device injection, etc.\n\n#### Image Service (server/images/)\nImplements CRI ImageService:\n- PullImage - download image\n- ImageStatus - check if image exists\n- RemoveImage - delete image\n- ImageFsInfo - get image filesystem info\n- ListImages - enumerate images\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Kubernetes to Containerd: The Complete Data Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Flow\n\n```\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ Kubernetes kubelet (process A)                                    │\n│                                                                   │\n│  func (m *kubeGenericRuntimeManager) RunPodSandbox() {           │\n│      req := &runtimeapi.RunPodSandboxRequest{ ... }              │\n│      resp, err := m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox(ctx, req)       │\n│  }                                                                │\n└──────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   │ gRPC call over Unix socket\n                   │ /run/containerd/containerd.sock\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ containerd daemon (process B)                                     │\n│                                                                   │\n│ func (c *criService) RunPodSandbox(ctx context.Context,          │\n│                          req *runtimeapi.RunPodSandboxRequest) {  │\n│     // 1. Validate request                                        │\n│     // 2. Generate IDs                                            │\n│     // 3. Create data structures                                  │\n│     // 4. Setup networking (CNI)                                  │\n│     // 5. Start sandbox container via task service                │\n│     // 6. Return response                                         │\n│ }                                                                 │\n└──────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   │ Calls containerd APIs\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ containerd core services (same daemon)                            │\n│                                                                   │\n│ ├─ snapshots.Snapshotter        (create filesystem layers)       │\n│ ├─ tasks.TasksService            (process management)            │\n│ ├─ containers.ContainersService  (container metadata)            │\n│ ├─ content.Store                 (image data)                    │\n│ └─ leases.LeasesService          (resource tracking)             │\n└──────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   │ Uses containerd-shim\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ containerd-shim (helper process per sandbox)                     │\n│                                                                   │\n│ ├─ Manages container processes                                   │\n│ ├─ Handles I/O (stdin/stdout/stderr)                             │\n│ ├─ Monitors process exit                                         │\n│ └─ Communicates with runtime (runc, kata, gvisor)               │\n└──────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n                   │ Calls runtime\n                   │\n                   ▼\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ OCI Runtime (runc, kata, gvisor, etc.)                            │\n│                                                                   │\n│ ├─ Creates namespaces (pid, ipc, uts, network, user)            │\n│ ├─ Sets up cgroups (resource limits)                            │\n│ ├─ Applies security context (SELinux, AppArmor)                 │\n│ ├─ Mounts root filesystem                                        │\n│ └─ Executes entry command in container                          │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### 3.2 Key Type Mappings\n\n| Kubernetes CRI Type | containerd Type | Location |\n|---|---|---|\n| `runtimeapi.PodSandboxConfig` | `sandbox.Sandbox.Metadata.Config` | store/sandbox/sandbox.go |\n| `runtimeapi.ContainerConfig` | `sandbox.Container.Metadata.Config` | store/container/container.go |\n| `runtimeapi.ContainerState` | `containerd.Container.Status()` | containerd API |\n| `runtimeapi.PodSandboxState` | `sandbox.Sandbox.Status.State` | store/sandbox/sandbox.go |\n| `runtimeapi.ImageSpec` | `images.Image` | containerd API |\n| `runtimeapi.Mount` | `mount.Mount` | containerd API |\n| `runtimeapi.Device` | `runc spec Device` | OCI spec |\n| `runtimeapi.LinuxContainerConfig` | `oci.Spec.Linux` | containerd/oci package |\n| `runtimeapi.LinuxPodSandboxConfig` | Platform-specific config | podsandbox/controller.go |\n\n### 3.3 Idempotency Pattern\n\nKubernetes gRPC operations are designed to be idempotent:\n\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StopPodSandbox(ctx context.Context,\n        req *runtimeapi.StopPodSandboxRequest) (*runtimeapi.StopPodSandboxResponse, error) {\n\n    // Get sandbox (returns nil if not found)\n    sandbox := c.sandboxStore.Get(req.PodSandboxId)\n    if sandbox == nil {\n        // Idempotent: already removed, return success\n        return &runtimeapi.StopPodSandboxResponse{}, nil\n    }\n\n    // Stop containers\n    // Stop sandbox\n\n    return &runtimeapi.StopPodSandboxResponse{}, nil\n}\n```\n\nThis means kubelet can safely retry on failures without worrying about double operations.\n\n### 3.4 Error Handling\n\nKubernetes expects specific error types:\n\n```go\n// From k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/errors\n\ntype Error struct {\n    Code string  // \"PodSandboxNotFound\", \"ContainerNotFound\", etc.\n    Msg  string\n}\n```\n\ncontainerd converts Go errors to these standard codes:\n\n```go\n// If sandbox not found:\nif sandbox == nil {\n    return nil, errdefs.WithNotFound(err)  // Maps to \"PodSandboxNotFound\"\n}\n\n// If invalid argument:\nif config == nil {\n    return nil, errdefs.WithInvalidArgument(err)  // Maps to \"Invalid\"\n}\n\n// If internal error:\nif err != nil {\n    return nil, errdefs.WithInternal(err)  // Maps to \"Internal\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Kubernetes Vendoring of containerd Types\n\n### 4.1 Vendored Containerd Packages\n\n**Location:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/`\n\n**Vendored Version:** v1.10.0 (from go.mod)\n\n**Direct containerd dependencies in kubernetes/go.mod:**\n```\ngithub.com/containerd/containerd/api v1.10.0\ngithub.com/containerd/errdefs v1.0.0\ngithub.com/containerd/log v0.1.0\ngithub.com/containerd/ttrpc v1.2.7\ngithub.com/containerd/typeurl/v2 v2.2.3\n```\n\n### 4.2 Vendored API Structure\n\n```\nkubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/\n├── types/\n│   ├── descriptor.pb.go      (OCI image descriptor)\n│   ├── platform.pb.go        (platform selectors)\n│   ├── mount.pb.go           (mount points)\n│   ├── event.pb.go           (event types)\n│   ├── metrics.pb.go         (metric definitions)\n│   ├── sandbox.pb.go         (sandbox types - NEW in 1.10)\n│   └── task/\n│       └── task.pb.go        (task/container types)\n│\n└── services/\n    ├── containers/v1/\n    │   ├── containers.pb.go\n    │   ├── containers_grpc.pb.go\n    │   └── containers_ttrpc.pb.go\n    ├── tasks/v1/\n    │   ├── tasks.pb.go\n    │   ├── tasks_grpc.pb.go\n    │   └── tasks_ttrpc.pb.go\n    └── version/v1/\n        ├── version.pb.go\n        ├── version_grpc.pb.go\n        └── version_ttrpc.pb.go\n```\n\n**Key fact:** Kubernetes vendors containerd's **API definitions only**, not the implementation. This provides type safety and version compatibility guarantees.\n\n### 4.3 Why Kubernetes Vendors containerd\n\n**Reason 1: Type Safety**\n- containerd API types are used in Kubernetes code\n- Vendoring ensures version compatibility\n- If containerd types changed, it would break Kubernetes\n\n**Reason 2: Version Control**\n- Kubernetes specifies exact containerd API version in go.mod\n- All Kubernetes releases have known compatible containerd API versions\n- Tests can verify compatibility\n\n**Reason 3: Avoiding Circular Dependencies**\n- containerd imports Kubernetes types (CRI proto)\n- Kubernetes imports containerd types (for integration)\n- Vendoring breaks the circle\n\n**Reason 4: Graceful Compatibility**\n- If containerd API breaks (major version bump)\n- Old Kubernetes versions still work with new containerd\n- Because Kubernetes has vendored the old API types\n\n### 4.4 Kubernetes Does NOT Directly Use Vendored containerd Implementation\n\n**Critical point:** Kubernetes vendors containerd **API types only**, not the implementation.\n\n```go\n// ✅ Kubernetes CAN use vendored types:\nimport \"github.com/containerd/containerd/api/types\"\nvar desc types.Descriptor\n\n// ❌ Kubernetes DOES NOT use vendored implementation:\n// NOT imported anywhere:\n// github.com/containerd/containerd/services/containers/v1\n// github.com/containerd/containerd/services/tasks/v1\n// (containerd implementation code)\n\n// Instead, Kubernetes communicates via gRPC:\nimport \"k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1\"\nvar client runtimev1.RuntimeServiceClient  // gRPC client\n```\n\n### 4.5 go.mod dependency graph\n\n```\nkubernetes/go.mod declares:\n    require github.com/containerd/containerd/api v1.10.0\n\nwhich vendorizes into:\n    vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/\n        api/\n            types/          ← Used by Kubernetes code\n            services/       ← Used by gRPC internally, not by Kubernetes\n```\n\n### 4.6 Used containerd API Types\n\nKubernetes actually references these vendored types in limited places:\n\n1. **Image handling (pkg/kubelet/images/):**\n   - `containerd/api/types.Descriptor` - OCI image descriptor\n\n2. **Statistics:**\n   - `containerd/api/types/metrics.MetricFamily` - metric definitions\n\n3. **Error compatibility:**\n   - `containerd/api/types` - error codes and status values\n\nBut **99%** of containerd interaction happens via gRPC with generated types from `k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/`.\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Complete Architecture Summary\n\n### 5.1 Three Layer Model\n\n**Layer 1: Kubernetes CRI Specification (Owned by Kubernetes)**\n- File: `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto`\n- Authority: Kubernetes community\n- Defines: RuntimeService and ImageService gRPC contracts\n- Protocol: gRPC + protobuf\n- Generated artifacts: Go types, gRPC stubs, interfaces\n\n**Layer 2: containerd Implementation (Owned by containerd project)**\n- Files: `plugins/cri/cri.go`, `internal/cri/server/*.go`\n- Implementation pattern: Plugin within containerd daemon\n- Maps CRI gRPC calls to containerd's core task/container APIs\n- Talks to: OCI runtimes (runc, kata, gvisor)\n\n**Layer 3: containerd Core APIs**\n- Services: ContainersService, TasksService, SnapshotsService\n- Abstraction over runtimes\n- Wire protocol: gRPC and TTRPC\n\n### 5.2 Data Flow\n\n```\nKubernetes Kubelet\n    ↓ gRPC call with runtimeapi.* types\ncontainerd CRI Plugin (gRPC handler)\n    ↓ Maps to containerd data structures\ncontainerd Core Services\n    ↓ Calls OCI runtime\nrunc / kata / gvisor\n    ↓ Manages actual processes/namespaces/cgroups\nLinux Kernel\n    ↓ Process execution\nContainer Process\n```\n\n### 5.3 Key Design Principles\n\n1. **Interface-Based Design**\n   - Kubernetes defines interface (RuntimeService)\n   - containerd implements interface\n   - Other runtimes (CRI-O, podman) also implement same interface\n\n2. **Idempotency**\n   - All write operations (Stop, Remove) are idempotent\n   - Safe to retry on network failures\n   - Kubernetes can retry without explicit error handling\n\n3. **State Separation**\n   - Kubernetes CRI API state (PodSandboxState) separate from\n   - containerd internal state (Task.Status)\n   - containerd maps internal state to CRI state\n\n4. **Resource Management**\n   - containerd uses leases to track resources\n   - Pod sandbox is a lease scope\n   - When pod is deleted, all resources under lease are cleanup\n\n5. **Pluggable Sandboxing**\n   - containerd supports multiple sandbox implementations\n   - Configured via runtime_handler\n   - Linux (runc) most common, but kata/gvisor available\n\n### 5.4 Version Compatibility Matrix\n\n| Kubernetes | CRI API | containerd | Tested? |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| 1.28 | v1 (v1alpha2) | 1.7+ | ✅ Yes |\n| 1.29 | v1 | 1.7+ | ✅ Yes |\n| 1.30 | v1 | 1.7+ | ✅ Yes |\n| 1.31 | v1 | 2.0+ | ✅ Yes |\n\nCRI API is stable (v1) and has been compatible since Kubernetes 1.23.\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Key Insights\n\n### 6.1 Why This Architecture Matters\n\n1. **Runtime Pluggability**: Kubernetes doesn't care if the runtime is containerd, CRI-O, or anything else that implements CRI. The abstraction is clean.\n\n2. **Version Independence**: Kubernetes and containerd have independent version cycles. They're loosely coupled via the gRPC interface.\n\n3. **Clear Responsibility Boundary**:\n   - Kubernetes: orchestration, scheduling, networking policy\n   - containerd: container lifecycle, image storage, runtime management\n\n4. **Security Isolation**: Kubernetes and container runtime run as separate processes. Kubernetes can't directly manipulate containers; it must request via gRPC.\n\n5. **Resource Efficiency**: Running multiple Kubernetes clusters on same machine with separate containerd daemons is possible.\n\n### 6.2 The Cost of Abstraction\n\n1. **gRPC Overhead**: Every container operation crosses process boundary (small but measurable latency)\n\n2. **State Duplication**: Both Kubernetes and containerd track pod/container state (they must stay in sync)\n\n3. **Error Handling**: gRPC errors must be mapped to Kubernetes error codes\n\n4. **Debugging Complexity**: Troubleshooting requires understanding two systems\n\n### 6.3 Common Operations Breakdown\n\n**Operation: Create and Start a Container**\n\n```\nKubernetes side (pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/):\n    1. Call RuntimeService.CreateContainer()\n       - gRPC to containerd\n       - containerd creates containerd.Container object\n       - Returns container_id\n\n    2. Call RuntimeService.StartContainer(container_id)\n       - gRPC to containerd\n       - containerd calls Container.NewTask()\n       - containerd-shim forks child process\n       - runc (OCI runtime) sets up namespaces, cgroups, mounts\n       - Entry command executes\n       - Returns when command starts (not when it exits)\n\nResult:\n    - Container running in kernel\n    - Process with isolated namespaces\n    - cgroup limiting resources\n    - Network namespace connected to pod network\n```\n\n**Operation: Stop and Remove a Container**\n\n```\nKubernetes side:\n    1. Call RuntimeService.StopContainer(container_id, timeout=30)\n       - gRPC to containerd\n       - containerd sends SIGTERM to container process\n       - Waits up to 30 seconds for process to exit\n       - If timeout, sends SIGKILL\n\n    2. Call RuntimeService.RemoveContainer(container_id)\n       - gRPC to containerd\n       - containerd deletes Container object\n       - Snapshot (filesystem) is deleted\n       - Container name is freed\n\nResult:\n    - All container resources cleaned up\n    - Filesystem snapshot deleted (space freed)\n    - Container can be recreated with same name\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: File Reference Guide\n\n### Kubernetes CRI API Files\n- **Main proto**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto` (2,129 lines)\n- **Generated types**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.pb.go` (~583 KB)\n- **Generated gRPC**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api_grpc.pb.go` (~79 KB)\n- **Go interfaces**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/services.go`\n- **Error types**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/errors/errors.go`\n\n### Kubernetes CRI Client\n- **Remote runtime client**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/pkg/kubelet/cri/remote/remote_runtime.go`\n- **Kubelet runtime manager**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`\n\n### containerd CRI Plugin Entry Point\n- **Plugin registration**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/plugins/cri/cri.go` (70 lines)\n\n### containerd CRI Service Implementation\n- **Main service**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/service.go` (1,200+ lines)\n- **Pod sandbox lifecycle**:\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/sandbox_run.go`\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/sandbox_stop.go`\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/sandbox_remove.go`\n- **Container lifecycle**:\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/container_create.go`\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/container_start.go`\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/container_stop.go`\n  - `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/container_remove.go`\n\n### containerd CRI Data Stores\n- **Sandbox store**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/store/sandbox/sandbox.go`\n- **Container store**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/store/container/container.go`\n\n### containerd Pod Sandbox Controller\n- **Linux sandbox**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/podsandbox/controller.go`\n- **Platform abstraction**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/podsandbox/` (12 files)\n\n### containerd Supporting Components\n- **Streaming server**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/streamingserver/`\n- **Event monitor**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/events/events.go`\n- **Image service**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/images/`\n- **Stats collector**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/containerd/internal/cri/server/stats_collector.go`\n\n### Kubernetes Vendored containerd Types\n- **Vendored location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/`\n- **API types**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/types/`\n- **Services**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/services/`\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes CRI is a masterclass in interface-based architecture. By defining a clear gRPC contract in `.proto` files, Kubernetes enables multiple container runtime implementations (containerd, CRI-O, etc.) to be plugged in without any dependency on Kubernetes implementation details.\n\ncontainerd's implementation demonstrates how to:\n1. Map high-level pod/container abstractions to lower-level task/process management\n2. Provide idempotent APIs for reliability\n3. Implement plugin architecture for extensibility\n4. Cleanly separate concerns (networking, storage, compute)\n\nThe vendoring of containerd types in Kubernetes ensures version compatibility while maintaining clean separation of concerns between orchestrator and runtime.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
